         </div>

       </tr>

      <p>
       <b>
        Asturian
       </b>
       (
       <span class="nowrap">
        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
          /
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">
            æ
           </span>
           <span title="'s' in 'sigh'">
            s
           </span>
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="'t' in 'tie'">
            t
           </span>
           <span title="/jʊər/: 'ure' in 'cure'">
            jʊər
           </span>
           <span title="/i/: 'y' in 'happy'">
            i
           </span>
           <span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">
            ə
           </span>
           <span title="'n' in 'nigh'">
            n
           </span>
          </span>
          /
         </a>
        </span>
       </span>
       ;
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Endonym" title="Endonym">
        autonym
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        asturianu
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Astur-Leonese" title="Help:IPA/Astur-Leonese">
         [astuˈɾjanu]
        </a>
       </span>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bable/asturiano_5-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-bable/asturiano-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       formerly also known as
       <i>
        bable
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Astur-Leonese" title="Help:IPA/Astur-Leonese">
         [ˈbaβle]
        </a>
       </span>
       ) is a
       <a href="/wiki/West_Iberian_languages" title="West Iberian languages">
        West Iberian
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Romance_language" title="Romance language">
        Romance language
       </a>
       spoken in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Principality_of_Asturias" title="Principality of Asturias">
        Principality of Asturias
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">
        Spain
       </a>
       . Asturian is part of a wider linguistic group, the
       <a href="/wiki/Astur-Leonese_languages" title="Astur-Leonese languages">
        Astur-Leonese languages
       </a>
       . The number of speakers is estimated at 100,000 (native) and 450,000 (second language).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There are three main variants in the Astur-Leonese language family: Western, Central, and Eastern. For historical and demographic reasons, the
       <a href="/wiki/Standard_language" title="Standard language">
        standard
       </a>
       is based on
       <a href="/wiki/Asturian_language#Central_Asturian" title="Asturian language">
        Central Asturian
       </a>
       . Asturian has a distinct
       <a href="/wiki/Grammar" title="Grammar">
        grammar
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Dictionary" title="Dictionary">
        dictionary
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Orthography" title="Orthography">
        orthography
       </a>
       . Regulated by the
       <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_the_Asturian_Language" title="Academy of the Asturian Language">
        Academy of the Asturian Language
       </a>
       , although it is not an
       <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">
        official language
       </a>
       of Spain
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       it is protected under the
       <a href="/wiki/Statute_of_Autonomy" title="Statute of Autonomy">
        Statute of Autonomy
       </a>
       and is an elective language in schools.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

       <div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" lang="en" xml:lang="en">
        <h2>
         Contents
        </h2>
       </div>

      <p>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
        History
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Asturian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map_Iberian_Peninsula_910-es.svg">
         <img alt="Multicolored map of the Iberian peninsula" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="569" data-file-width="818" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Map_Iberian_Peninsula_910-es.svg/200px-Map_Iberian_Peninsula_910-es.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Map_Iberian_Peninsula_910-es.svg/300px-Map_Iberian_Peninsula_910-es.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Map_Iberian_Peninsula_910-es.svg/400px-Map_Iberian_Peninsula_910-es.svg.png 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Map_Iberian_Peninsula_910-es.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Kingdom of Asturias about 910 AD, after the reign of King
         <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_III_of_Asturias" title="Alfonso III of Asturias">
          Alfonso III of Asturias
         </a>
         (848–910)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Astur-Leonese is the historical language of Asturias, portions of the Spanish provinces of
       <a href="/wiki/Le%C3%B3n,_Spain" title="León, Spain">
        León
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Zamora,_Spain" title="Zamora, Spain">
        Zamora
       </a>
       and the area surrounding
       <a href="/wiki/Miranda_do_Douro" title="Miranda do Douro">
        Miranda do Douro
       </a>
       in northeastern Portugal.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Map_9-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Map-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Like the other Romance languages of the Iberian peninsula, it evolved from
       <a href="/wiki/Vulgar_Latin" title="Vulgar Latin">
        Vulgar Latin
       </a>
       during the
       <a href="/wiki/Early_Middle_Ages" title="Early Middle Ages">
        early Middle Ages
       </a>
       . Asturian was closely linked with the
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Asturias" title="Kingdom of Asturias">
        Kingdom of Asturias
       </a>
       (718–910) and the ensuing Leonese kingdom. The language had contributions from pre-Roman languages spoken by the
       <a href="/wiki/Astures" title="Astures">
        Astures
       </a>
       , an Iberian
       <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">
        Celtic
       </a>
       tribe, and the post-Roman
       <a href="/wiki/Germanic_languages" title="Germanic languages">
        Germanic languages
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Visigoths" title="Visigoths">
        Visigoths
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Suevi" title="Suevi">
        Suevi
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The transition from Latin to Asturian was slow and gradual; for a long time they co-existed in a
       <a href="/wiki/Diglossia" title="Diglossia">
        diglossic
       </a>
       relationship, first in the Kingdom of Asturias and later in that of Asturias and Leon. During the 12th, 13th and part of the 14th centuries Astur-Leonese was used in the kingdom's official documents, with many examples of agreements, donations, wills and commercial contracts from that period onwards. Although there are no extant literary works written in Asturian from this period, some books (such as the
       <i>
        Llibru d'Alexandre
       </i>
       and the 1155
       <i>
        Fueru d'Avilés
       </i>
       )
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FueruAviles_11-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FueruAviles-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       had Asturian sources.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
        Castilian Spanish
       </a>
       arrived in the area during the 14th century, when the central administration sent emissaries and functionaries to political and ecclesiastical offices. Asturian codification of the Astur-Leonese spoken in the Asturian Autonomous Community became a modern language with the founding of the Academy of the Asturian Language (
       <i>
        Academia Asturiana de la Llingua
       </i>
       ) in 1980. The
       <a href="/wiki/Leonese_dialect" title="Leonese dialect">
        Leonese dialects
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mirandese" title="Mirandese">
        Mirandese
       </a>
       are linguistically close to Asturian.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Status_and_legislation">
        Status and legislation
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Asturian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Status and legislation">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Efforts have been made since 1974 to protect and promote Asturian.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 1994, there were 100,000 native speakers and 450,000
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       second-language speakers able to speak (or understand) Asturian.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, the language is endangered; there has been a steep decline in the number of speakers over the last century. Law 1/93 of March 23 on the Use and Promotion of the Asturian Language addresses the issue, and according to article four of the Asturias Statute of Autonomy:
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bable/asturiano_5-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-bable/asturiano-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       "The Asturian language will enjoy protection. Its use, teaching and diffusion in the media will be furthered, whilst its local dialects and voluntary apprenticeship will always be respected".
      </p>
      <p>
       Asturian, however, is in a legally hazy position. The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_Constitution" title="Spanish Constitution">
        Spanish Constitution
       </a>
       has not been fully applied regarding the official recognition of languages in the autonomous communities. The ambiguity of the Statute of Autonomy, which recognises the existence of Asturian but does not give it the same status as Spanish, leaves the door open to benign neglect. However, since 1 August 2001 Asturian has been covered under the
       <a href="/wiki/European_Charter_for_Regional_or_Minority_Languages" title="European Charter for Regional or Minority Languages">
        European Charter for Regional or Minority Languages
       </a>
       ' "safeguard and promote" clause.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eucharter_3-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-eucharter-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       A 1983 survey
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       indicated 100,000 native Asturian speakers (12 percent of the Asturian population) and 250,000 who could speak or understand Asturian as a second language. A similar survey in 1991 found that 44 percent of the population (about 450,000 people) could speak Asturian, with from 60,000 to 80,000 able to read and write it. An additional 24 percent of the Asturian population said that they understood the language, for a total of about 68 percent of the Asturian population.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       At the end of the 20th century, the Academia de la Llingua Asturiana (Academy of the Asturian Language) attempted to provide the language with tools needed to enhance its survival: a
       <a href="/wiki/Grammar" title="Grammar">
        grammar
       </a>
       , a
       <a href="/wiki/Dictionary" title="Dictionary">
        dictionary
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Periodicals" title="Periodicals">
        periodicals
       </a>
       ; a new generation of Asturian writers have also championed the language.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span id="Historical.2C_social_and_cultural_aspects">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Historical,_social_and_cultural_aspects">
        Historical, social and cultural aspects
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Asturian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Historical, social and cultural aspects">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Literary_history">
        <span id="History_of_the_literature">
        </span>
        Literary history
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Asturian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Literary history">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Marirreguera.jpg">
         <img alt="Sketch of man wearing a crown and a white, ruffled collar" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1191" data-file-width="951" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Marirreguera.jpg/150px-Marirreguera.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Marirreguera.jpg/225px-Marirreguera.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Marirreguera.jpg/300px-Marirreguera.jpg 2x" width="150"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Marirreguera.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         19th-century sketch of 17th-century author
         <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3n_de_Marirreguera" title="Antón de Marirreguera">
          Antón de Marirreguera
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Francisco_de_Goya_y_Lucientes_-_Gaspar_Melchor_de_Jovellanos.jpg">
         <img alt="Portrait of a man seated at a desk, cheek resting on his hand" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3051" data-file-width="1939" height="236" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Francisco_de_Goya_y_Lucientes_-_Gaspar_Melchor_de_Jovellanos.jpg/150px-Francisco_de_Goya_y_Lucientes_-_Gaspar_Melchor_de_Jovellanos.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Francisco_de_Goya_y_Lucientes_-_Gaspar_Melchor_de_Jovellanos.jpg/225px-Francisco_de_Goya_y_Lucientes_-_Gaspar_Melchor_de_Jovellanos.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Francisco_de_Goya_y_Lucientes_-_Gaspar_Melchor_de_Jovellanos.jpg/300px-Francisco_de_Goya_y_Lucientes_-_Gaspar_Melchor_de_Jovellanos.jpg 2x" width="150"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Francisco_de_Goya_y_Lucientes_-_Gaspar_Melchor_de_Jovellanos.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Jurist" title="Jurist">
          Jurist
         </a>
         and
         <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Enlightenment_literature" title="Spanish Enlightenment literature">
          neoclassical author
         </a>
         <a href="/wiki/Gaspar_Melchor_de_Jovellanos" title="Gaspar Melchor de Jovellanos">
          Gaspar Melchor de Jovellanos
         </a>
         (1744–1811), who envisaged the
         <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_the_Asturian_Language" title="Academy of the Asturian Language">
          Academy of the Asturian Language
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Asturian_literature" title="Asturian literature">
        Asturian literature
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Although some 10th-century documents have the linguistic features of Asturian, numerous examples (such as writings by
       <a href="/wiki/Notary_public" title="Notary public">
        notaries
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Contract" title="Contract">
        contracts
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Will_(law)" title="Will (law)">
        wills
       </a>
       ) begin in the 13th century.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ciemen.org_18-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ciemen.org-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Early examples are the 1085
       <i>
        Fuero de Avilés
       </i>
       (the oldest parchment preserved in Asturias)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and the 13th-century
       <i>
        Fuero de Oviedo
       </i>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Leonese_dialect" title="Leonese dialect">
        Leonese
       </a>
       version of the
       <i>
        Fueru Xulgu
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The 13th-century documents were the laws for towns, cities and the general population.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ciemen.org_18-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-ciemen.org-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       By the second half of the 16th century, documents were written in Castilian, backed by the
       <a href="/wiki/Trast%C3%A1maran_Castile" title="Trastámaran Castile">
        Trastámara dynasty
       </a>
       and making the civil and ecclesiastical arms of the rincipality Castilian. Although the Asturian language disappeared from written texts during the
       <i>
        sieglos escuros
       </i>
       (dark centuries), it survived orally. The only written mention during this time is from a 1555 work by
       <a href="/wiki/Hern%C3%A1n_N%C3%BA%C3%B1ez" title="Hernán Núñez">
        Hernán Núñez
       </a>
       about proverbs and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adages" title="Adages">
        adages
       </a>
       : " ... in a large copy of rare languages, as Portuguese, Galician, Asturian, Catalan, Valencian, French, Tuscan ... ".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
        <a href="#cite_note-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Modern Asturian literature began in 1605 with the clergyman
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3n_Gonz%C3%A1lez_Reguera" title="Antón González Reguera">
        Antón González Reguera
       </a>
       and continued until the 18th century (when it produced, according to Ruiz de la Peña in 1981, a literature comparable to that in Asturias in Castilian).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 1744,
       <a href="/wiki/Gaspar_Melchor_de_Jovellanos" title="Gaspar Melchor de Jovellanos">
        Gaspar Melchor de Jovellanos
       </a>
       wrote about the historic and cultural value of Asturian, urging the compilation of a dictionary and a grammar and the creation of a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Language_regulator" title="Language regulator">
        language academy
       </a>
       . Notable writers included
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Francisco_Bernaldo_de_Quir%C3%B3s_Benavides" title="Francisco Bernaldo de Quirós Benavides">
        Francisco Bernaldo de Quirós Benavides
       </a>
       (1675),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Josefa_Jovellanos" title="Josefa Jovellanos">
        Xosefa Xovellanos
       </a>
       (1745),
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Xuan_Gonz%C3%A1lez_Villar_y_Fuertes&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Xuan González Villar y Fuertes (page does not exist)">
        Xuan González Villar y Fuertes
       </a>
       (1746),
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Caveda_y_Nava&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="José Caveda y Nava (page does not exist)">
        Xosé Caveda y Nava
       </a>
       (1796),
       <a href="/wiki/Juan_Mar%C3%ADa_Acebal" title="Juan María Acebal">
        Xuan María Acebal
       </a>
       (1815),
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Teodoro_Cuesta&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Teodoro Cuesta (page does not exist)">
        Teodoro Cuesta
       </a>
       (1829), Xosé Benigno García González,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Marcos_del_Torniello&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Marcos del Torniello (page does not exist)">
        Marcos del Torniello
       </a>
       (1853),
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Bernardo_Acevedo_y_Huelves&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Bernardo Acevedo y Huelves (page does not exist)">
        Bernardo Acevedo y Huelves
       </a>
       (1849),
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Pin_de_Pr%C3%ADa&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Pin de Pría (page does not exist)">
        Pin de Pría
       </a>
       (1864), Galo Fernández and
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Fern%C3%A1n_Coronas&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Fernán Coronas (page does not exist)">
        Fernán Coronas
       </a>
       (1884).
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1974, a movement for the language's acceptance and use began in Asturias. Based on ideas of the Asturian association
       <a href="/wiki/Conceyu_Bable" title="Conceyu Bable">
        Conceyu Bable
       </a>
       about Asturian language and culture, a plan was developed for the acceptance and modernization of the language that led to the 1980 creation of the Academy of the Asturian Language with the approval of the Asturias regional council.
       <i>
        El Surdimientu
       </i>
       (the Awakening) authors such as
       <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Asur" title="Manuel Asur">
        Manuel Asur
       </a>
       <i>
        (Cancios y poemes pa un riscar)
       </i>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Xuan_Bello" title="Xuan Bello">
        Xuan Bello
       </a>
       <i>
        (El llibru vieyu)
       </i>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Adolfo_Camilo_D%C3%ADaz" title="Adolfo Camilo Díaz">
        Adolfo Camilo Díaz
       </a>
       <i>
        (Añada pa un güeyu muertu)
       </i>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Pablo_Ant%C3%B3n_Mar%C3%ADn_Estrada" title="Pablo Antón Marín Estrada">
        Pablo Antón Marín Estrada
       </a>
       <i>
        (Les hores)
       </i>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Xandru_Fern%C3%A1ndez" title="Xandru Fernández">
        Xandru Fernández
       </a>
       <i>
        (Les ruines)
       </i>
       ,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Lourdes_%C3%81lvarez&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Lourdes Álvarez (page does not exist)">
        Lourdes Álvarez
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mart%C3%ADn_L%C3%B3pez-Vega" title="Martín López-Vega">
        Martín López-Vega
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Miguel_Rojo&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Miguel Rojo (page does not exist)">
        Miguel Rojo
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Lluis_Ant%C3%B3n_Gonz%C3%A1lez" title="Lluis Antón González">
        Lluis Antón González
       </a>
       broke from the Asturian-Leonese tradition of rural themes, moral messages and dialogue-style writing. Currently, the Asturian language has about 150 annual publications.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Use_and_distribution">
        <span id="Geographical_distribution">
        </span>
        Use and distribution
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Asturian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Use and distribution">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Astur-Leonese's geographic area exceeds Asturias, and that the language known as Leonese in the
       <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_communities_of_Spain" title="Autonomous communities of Spain">
        autonomous community
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Castile_and_Le%C3%B3n" title="Castile and León">
        Castile and León
       </a>
       is basically the same as the Asturian spoken in Asturias. The
       <a href="/wiki/Astur-Leonese_languages" title="Astur-Leonese languages">
        Asturian-Leonese linguistic domain
       </a>
       covers most of the principality of Asturias, the northern and western
       <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Le%C3%B3n" title="Province of León">
        province of León
       </a>
       , the northeastern
       <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Zamora" title="Province of Zamora">
        province of Zamora
       </a>
       (both in Castile and León), western
       <a href="/wiki/Cantabria" title="Cantabria">
        Cantabria
       </a>
       and the Miranda do Douro region in the eastern
       <a href="/wiki/Bragan%C3%A7a_District" title="Bragança District">
        Bragança District
       </a>
       of Portugal.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Toponymy">
        Toponymy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Asturian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Toponymy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Toponimia_asturiana_2017.svg">
         <img alt="Color-coded map of Asturias, with most Asturian place-names official" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="413" data-file-width="778" height="159" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Toponimia_asturiana_2017.svg/300px-Toponimia_asturiana_2017.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Toponimia_asturiana_2017.svg/450px-Toponimia_asturiana_2017.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Toponimia_asturiana_2017.svg/600px-Toponimia_asturiana_2017.svg.png 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Toponimia_asturiana_2017.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Asturian place-name status, 2017
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #0000FF; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          <i>
           Conceyos
          </i>
          (municipalities) whose traditional place names have been codified
         </div>
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #7FFFD4; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          <i>
           Conceyos
          </i>
          which have applied for approval
         </div>
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #006400; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          <i>
           Conceyos
          </i>
          which have not applied
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Traditional, popular place names of the principality's towns are supported by the law on usage of Asturian, the principality’s 2003–07 plan for establishing the language
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
        <a href="#cite_note-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and the work of the
       <i>
        Xunta Asesora de Toponimia
       </i>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
        <a href="#cite_note-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       which researches and confirms the Asturian names of requesting villages, towns,
       <i>
        conceyos
       </i>
       and cities (50 of 78
       <i>
        conceyos
       </i>
       as of 2012).
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Dialects">
        <span id="Dialectal_variation">
        </span>
        <span id="Western_Asturian">
        </span>
        <span id="Central_Asturian">
        </span>
        <span id="Eastern_Asturian">
        </span>
        <span id="Transitional_varieties">
        </span>
        Dialects
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Asturian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Dialects">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Asturian_linguistic_areas.PNG">
         <img alt="Color-coded map of Asturias" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="824" data-file-width="993" height="232" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Asturian_linguistic_areas.PNG/280px-Asturian_linguistic_areas.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Asturian_linguistic_areas.PNG/420px-Asturian_linguistic_areas.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Asturian_linguistic_areas.PNG/560px-Asturian_linguistic_areas.PNG 2x" width="280"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Asturian_linguistic_areas.PNG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Asturian dialects: western, central and eastern
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Linguistic_map_of_asturian_es.svg">
         <img alt="Two maps, large- and small-scale" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="350" data-file-width="140" height="700" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Linguistic_map_of_asturian_es.svg/280px-Linguistic_map_of_asturian_es.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Linguistic_map_of_asturian_es.svg/420px-Linguistic_map_of_asturian_es.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Linguistic_map_of_asturian_es.svg/560px-Linguistic_map_of_asturian_es.svg.png 2x" width="280"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Linguistic_map_of_asturian_es.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Large- and small-scale maps of the Asturian-speaking region
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Asturian has several dialects. Regulated by the Academia de la Llingua Asturiana, it is mainly spoken in Asturias (except in the west, where
       <a href="/wiki/Galician-Asturian" title="Galician-Asturian">
        Galician-Asturian
       </a>
       is spoken). The dialect spoken in the adjoining area of
       <a href="/wiki/Castile_and_Le%C3%B3n" title="Castile and León">
        Castile and León
       </a>
       is known as
       <a href="/wiki/Leonese_dialect" title="Leonese dialect">
        Leonese
       </a>
       . Asturian is traditionally divided into three dialectal areas, sharing traits with the dialect spoken in León:
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
        <a href="#cite_note-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       western, central and eastern. The dialects are mutually intelligible. Central Asturian, with the most speakers (more than 80 percent) is the basis for standard Asturian. The first Asturian grammar was published in 1998, and the first dictionary in 2000.
      </p>
      <p>
       Western Asturian is spoken between the
       <a href="/wiki/Navia_(river)" title="Navia (river)">
        Navia
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Nal%C3%B3n_(river)" title="Nalón (river)">
        Nalón
       </a>
       Rivers, in the west of the province of León (where it is known as Leonese) and in the provinces of Zamora and
       <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Salamanca" title="Province of Salamanca">
        Salamanca
       </a>
       . Feminine plurals end in
       <i>
        -as
       </i>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/Diphthong#Falling_and_rising" title="Diphthong">
        falling diphthongs
       </a>
       /ei/ and /ou/ are maintained.
      </p>
      <p>
       Central Asturian is spoken between the
       <a href="/wiki/Sella_River_(Bay_of_Biscay)" title="Sella River (Bay of Biscay)">
        Sella River
       </a>
       and the mouth of the Nalón River in Asturias and north of León. The model for the written language, it is characterized by feminine plurals ending in
       <i>
        -es
       </i>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Monophthongization" title="Monophthongization">
        monophthongization
       </a>
       of /ou/ and /ei/ into /o/ and /e/ and the
       <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_gender" title="Grammatical gender">
        neutral gender
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-neutro_materia_26-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-neutro_materia-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       in adjectives modifying uncountable nouns (
       <i>
        lleche frío
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        carne tienro
       </i>
       ).
      </p>
      <p>
       Eastern Asturian is spoken between the Sella River,
       <a href="/wiki/Llanes" title="Llanes">
        Llanes
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Cabrales" title="Cabrales">
        Cabrales
       </a>
       . The dialect is characterized by the
       <a href="/wiki/Debuccalization" title="Debuccalization">
        debuccalization
       </a>
       of word-initial /f/ to [
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_glottal_fricative" title="Voiceless glottal fricative">
         h
        </a>
       </span>
       ], written ⟨
       <a href="/wiki/Dot_(diacritic)" title="Dot (diacritic)">
        ḥ
       </a>
       ⟩ (
       <i>
        ḥoguera
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        ḥacer
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        ḥigos
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        ḥornu
       </i>
       instead of
       <i>
        foguera
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        facer
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        figos
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        fornu
       </i>
       ; feminine plurals ending in
       <i>
        -as
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        ḥab
        <b>
         a
        </b>
        s
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        ḥormig
        <b>
         a
        </b>
        s
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        ḥiy
        <b>
         a
        </b>
        s
       </i>
       , except in eastern towns, where
       <i>
        -es
       </i>
       is kept:
       <i>
        ḥabes
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        ḥormigues
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        ḥiyes
       </i>
       ); the shifting of word-final
       <i>
        -e
       </i>
       to
       <i>
        -i
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        xenti
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        tardi
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        ḥuenti
       </i>
       ); retention of the neutral gender
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-neutro_materia_26-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-neutro_materia-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       in some areas, with the ending
       <i>
        -u
       </i>
       instead of
       <i>
        -o
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        agua friu
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        xenti güenu
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        ropa tendíu
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        carne guisáu
       </i>
       ), and a distinction between direct and indirect objects in first- and second-person singular pronouns (direct
       <i>
        me
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        te
       </i>
       vs. indirect
       <i>
        mi
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        ti
       </i>
       ) in some municipalities bordering the Sella River:
       <i>
        busquéte (a ti) y alcontréte/busquéti les llaves y alcontrétiles
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        llévame (a mi) la fesoria en carru
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Asturian forms a
       <a href="/wiki/Dialect_continuum" title="Dialect continuum">
        dialect continuum
       </a>
       with
       <a href="/wiki/Cantabrian_dialect" title="Cantabrian dialect">
        Cantabrian
       </a>
       in the east and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eonavian" title="Eonavian">
        Eonavian
       </a>
       in the west.
       <a href="/wiki/Cantabrian_dialect" title="Cantabrian dialect">
        Cantabrian
       </a>
       or
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monta%C3%B1%C3%A9s" title="Montañés">
        Montañés
       </a>
       is spoken in eastern Asturias and portions of
       <a href="/wiki/Cantabria" title="Cantabria">
        Cantabria
       </a>
       (the
       <a href="/wiki/Valles_Pasiegos" title="Valles Pasiegos">
        Pas
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Soba,_Cantabria" title="Soba, Cantabria">
        Soba
       </a>
       Valleys). Cantabrian was listed in the 2009
       <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">
        UNESCO
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Red_Book_of_Endangered_Languages" title="Red Book of Endangered Languages">
        Atlas of the World's Languages in Danger
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unesco_27-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-unesco-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The inclusion of Eonavian (spoken in western Asturias, bordering Galicia) in the
       <a href="/wiki/Galician_language" title="Galician language">
        Galician language
       </a>
       is controversial, since it has traits in common with western Asturian.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Linguistic_description">
        Linguistic description
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Asturian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Linguistic description">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Asturian is one of the
       <a href="/wiki/Astur-Leonese_languages" title="Astur-Leonese languages">
        Astur-Leonese languages
       </a>
       which form part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Romance_languages" title="Iberian Romance languages">
        Iberian Romance languages
       </a>
       , close to
       <a href="/wiki/Galician-Portuguese" title="Galician-Portuguese">
        Galician-Portuguese
       </a>
       and Castilian and further removed from
       <a href="/wiki/Navarro-Aragonese" title="Navarro-Aragonese">
        Navarro-Aragonese
       </a>
       . It is an
       <a href="/wiki/Inflection" title="Inflection">
        inflecting
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Fusional_language" title="Fusional language">
        fusional
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Head-directionality_parameter" title="Head-directionality parameter">
        head-initial
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Dependent-marking_language" title="Dependent-marking language">
        dependent-marking language
       </a>
       . Its word order is
       <a href="/wiki/Subject%E2%80%93verb%E2%80%93object" title="Subject–verb–object">
        subject–verb–object
       </a>
       (in declarative sentences without
       <a href="/wiki/Topicalization" title="Topicalization">
        topicalization
       </a>
       ).
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Phonology">
        Phonology
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Asturian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Phonology">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Vowels">
        Vowels
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Asturian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Vowels">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       Asturian distinguishes five vowel phonemes (these same ones are found in
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_phonology#Vowels" title="Spanish phonology">
        Spanish
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Aragonese_language#Vowels" title="Aragonese language">
        Aragonese
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Sardinian_language#Vowels" title="Sardinian language">
        Sardinian
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Basque_language#Vowels" title="Basque language">
        Basque
       </a>
       ), according to three degrees of vowel openness (close, mid and open) and backness (front, central and back).
      </p>
      <table class="wikitable" style="text-align:center;">
       <tr>
        <th>

         </a>

      <ul>

        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /b, d, ɡ/
        </span>
        may be
        <a href="/wiki/Lenition" title="Lenition">
         lenited
        </a>
        in certain environments.
       </li>
       <li>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /n/
        </span>
        is pronounced
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [
         <a href="/wiki/Velar_nasal" title="Velar nasal">
          ŋ
         </a>
         ]
        </span>
        in coda position.
       </li>
       <li>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /ɡ/
        </span>
        is usually pronounced as a voiced fricative word-initially.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Writing">
        Writing
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Asturian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Writing">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">
        Latin
       </a>
       alphabet was used in the earliest Asturian texts. Although the Academia de la Llingua Asturiana published orthographic rules in 1981,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Normes_28-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Normes-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
       different spelling rules are used in
       <a href="/wiki/Terra_de_Miranda" title="Terra de Miranda">
        Terra de Miranda
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">
        Portugal
       </a>
       ).
      </p>
      <p>
       Asturian orthography is based on a five-vowel system (/a e i o u/), with three aperture degrees. It has the following consonants:
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /p t tʃ k b d ʝ ɡ f θ s ʃ m n ɲ l ʎ r ɾ/
       </span>
       . The phenomenon of
       <i>
        -u
       </i>
       <a href="/wiki/Metaphony_(Romance_languages)" title="Metaphony (Romance languages)">
        metaphony
       </a>
       is uncommon, as are decrescent diphthongs (/
       <i>
        ei
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        ou
       </i>
       /, usually in the west). Although they can be written,
       <i>
        ḷḷ
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/%E1%B8%B6" title="Ḷ">
         che vaqueira
        </a>
       </i>
       , formerly represented as "
       <i>
        ts
       </i>
       ") and the eastern
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Dot_(diacritic)" title="Dot (diacritic)">
         ḥ
        </a>
       </i>
       aspiration (also represented as "
       <i>
        h.
       </i>
       " and corresponding to
       <i>
        ll
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        f
       </i>
       ) are absent from this model. Asturian has triple gender distinction in the
       <a href="/wiki/Adjective" title="Adjective">
        adjective
       </a>
       , feminine plurals with
       <i>
        -es
       </i>
       , verb endings with
       <i>
        -es, -en, -íes, íen
       </i>
       and lacks
       <a href="/wiki/Present_perfect" title="Present perfect">
        compound tenses
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Normes_28-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Normes-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
       (or
       <a href="/wiki/Periphrasis" title="Periphrasis">
        periphrasis
       </a>
       constructed with "
       <i>
        tener
       </i>
       ").
      </p>

      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Digraphs">
        Digraphs
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Asturian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Digraphs">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hache_y_hache_aspirada.png">
         <img alt="Non-italicized and italicized upper- and lowercase H, with and without under-dotting" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="732" data-file-width="1140" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Hache_y_hache_aspirada.png/220px-Hache_y_hache_aspirada.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Hache_y_hache_aspirada.png/330px-Hache_y_hache_aspirada.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Hache_y_hache_aspirada.png/440px-Hache_y_hache_aspirada.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hache_y_hache_aspirada.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Asturian H and Ḥ
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Che_vaqueira.png">
         <img alt="Italicized and non-italicized upper- and lowercase Ḷ" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="256" data-file-width="280" height="201" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Che_vaqueira.png/220px-Che_vaqueira.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/4a/Che_vaqueira.png 1.5x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Che_vaqueira.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Asturian Ḷ
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Asturian has several
       <a href="/wiki/Digraph_(orthography)" title="Digraph (orthography)">
        digraphs
       </a>
       , some of which have their own names.
      </p>
      <table class="wikitable">
       <tr>
        <th>
         Digraph
        </th>
        <th>
         Name
        </th>
        <th>
         Phoneme
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         ch
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          che
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /t͡ʃ/
         </span>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         gu (+ e, i)
        </td>
        <td>
         (
         <i>
          gue u
         </i>
         )
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /ɡ/
         </span>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         ll
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          elle
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /ʎ/
         </span>
        </td>
       </tr>

          /k/
         </span>
        </td>
       </tr>

         </span>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>

         </span>

         </i>

       </tr>
       <tr>

        </td>

         (
         <i>

         </i>
         )
        </td>

         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /ɟ͡ʝ/
         </span>
         <i>
          (dialectal)
         </i>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Dialectal_spellings">
        Dialectal spellings
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Asturian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Dialectal spellings">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       The letter
       <i>
        h
       </i>
       and the digraph
       <i>
        ll
       </i>
       can have their sound changed to represent dialectal pronunciation by under-dotting the letters, resulting in
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Dot_(diacritic)" title="Dot (diacritic)">
         ḥ
        </a>
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/%E1%B8%B6" title="Ḷ">
         digraph ḷḷ
        </a>
       </i>
      </p>
      <table class="wikitable">
       <tr>
        <th>
         Normal
        </th>
        <th>
         Pronunciation
        </th>
        <th>
         Dotted
        </th>
        <th>
         Pronunciation
        </th>
        <th>
         Examples
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         ll
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /ʎ/
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/%E1%B8%B6" title="Ḷ">
          ḷ
         </a>
         ḷ
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /t͡s/
         </span>
         ,
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /ɖʐ/
         </span>
         ,
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /ɖ/
         </span>
         and
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /ʈʂ/
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          ḷḷeite
         </i>
         ,
         <i>
          ḷḷinu
         </i>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         h
        </td>
        <td>
         –
        </td>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Dot_(diacritic)" title="Dot (diacritic)">
          ḥ
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /h/
         </span>
         ,
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /x/
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          ḥou
         </i>
         ,
         <i>
          ḥenu
         </i>
         ,
         <i>
          ḥuera
         </i>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <ul>
       <li>
        The "
        <i>
         ḥ
        </i>
        " is common in eastern Asturian place names and in words beginning with
        <i>
         f
        </i>
        ;
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gramática_de_la_llingua_29-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Gramática_de_la_llingua-29">
          [29]
         </a>
        </sup>
        workarounds such as
        <i>
         h.
        </i>
        and
        <i>
         l.l
        </i>
        were used in the past for printing.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Grammar">
        Grammar
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Asturian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Grammar">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Diccionariualla.jpg">
         <img alt="Open dictionary and smaller books, with title on spine in an inset" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="2560" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Diccionariualla.jpg/250px-Diccionariualla.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Diccionariualla.jpg/375px-Diccionariualla.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Diccionariualla.jpg/500px-Diccionariualla.jpg 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Diccionariualla.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Asturian dictionary, published by the Academy of the Asturian Language
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Asturian grammar is similar to that of other Romance languages. Nouns have three
       <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_gender" title="Grammatical gender">
        genders
       </a>
       (masculine feminine and neuter), two
       <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_number" title="Grammatical number">
        numbers
       </a>
       (singular and plural) and no
       <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_case" title="Grammatical case">
        cases
       </a>
       . Adjectives may have a third, neuter gender, a phenomenon known as matter-neutrality.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gramática_de_la_llingua_29-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Gramática_de_la_llingua-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Verbs agree with their subjects in
       <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_person" title="Grammatical person">
        person
       </a>
       (first, second, or third) and number, and are conjugated to indicate
       <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_mood" title="Grammatical mood">
        mood
       </a>
       (indicative, subjunctive, conditional or imperative),
       <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_tense" title="Grammatical tense">
        tense
       </a>
       (often present or past; different moods allow different tenses), and
       <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_aspect" title="Grammatical aspect">
        aspect
       </a>
       (perfective or imperfective).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gramática_de_la_llingua_29-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Gramática_de_la_llingua-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Morphology">
        <span id="Morphological_features">
        </span>
        Morphology
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Asturian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Morphology">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Gender">
        Gender
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Asturian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Gender">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       Asturian is the only western Romance language with three genders:
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Masculine_(grammar)" title="Masculine (grammar)">
         masculine
        </a>
        ,
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Feminine_(grammar)" title="Feminine (grammar)">
         feminine
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_gender" title="Grammatical gender">
         neuter
        </a>
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <i>
         Masculine nouns
        </i>
        usually end in
        <i>
         -u
        </i>
        , sometimes in
        <i>
         -e
        </i>
        or a consonant:
        <i>
         el tiempu
        </i>
        (time, weather),
        <i>
         l’home
        </i>
        (man),
        <i>
         el pantalón
        </i>
        (trousers),
        <i>
         el xeitu
        </i>
        (way, mode).
       </li>
       <li>
        <i>
         Feminine nouns
        </i>
        usually end in
        <i>
         -a
        </i>
        , sometimes
        <i>
         -e
        </i>
        :
        <i>
         la casa
        </i>
        (house),
        <i>
         la xente
        </i>
        (people),
        <i>
         la nueche
        </i>
        (night).
       </li>
       <li>
        <i>
         Neuter nouns
        </i>
        may have any ending. Asturian has three types of neuters:
        <ul>
         <li>
          <i>
           Masculine neuters
          </i>
          have a masculine form and take a masculine article:
          <i>
           el fierro vieyo
          </i>
          (old iron).
         </li>
         <li>
          <i>
           Feminine neuters
          </i>
          have a feminine form and take a feminine article:
          <i>
           la lleche frío
          </i>
          (cold milk).
         </li>
         <li>
          <i>
           Pure neuters
          </i>
          are
          <a href="/wiki/Nominal_group_(functional_grammar)" title="Nominal group (functional grammar)">
           nominal groups
          </a>
          with an adjective and neuter pronoun:
          <i>
           lo guapo d’esti asuntu ye...
          </i>
          (the interesting [thing] about this issue is ...).
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Adjectives are modified by gender. Most adjectives have three endings:
       <i>
        -u
       </i>
       (masculine),
       <i>
        -a
       </i>
       (feminine) and
       <i>
        -o
       </i>
       (neuter):
       <i>
        El vasu ta frí
        <u>
         u
        </u>
       </i>
       (the glass is cold),
       <i>
        tengo la mano frí
        <u>
         a
        </u>
       </i>
       (my hand is cold),
       <i>
        l’agua ta frí
        <u>
         o
        </u>
       </i>
       (the water is cold)
      </p>
      <p>
       Neuter nouns are abstract, collective and uncountable nouns. They have no plural, except when they are used metaphorically or
       <a href="/wiki/Abstract_and_concrete" title="Abstract and concrete">
        concretised
       </a>
       and lose this gender:
       <i>
        l
        <u>
         es
        </u>
        agü
        <u>
         es
        </u>
        tán frí
        <u>
         es
        </u>
       </i>
       (Waters are cold).
       <i>
        Tien el pel
        <u>
         o
        </u>
        rox
        <u>
         o
        </u>
       </i>
       (He has red hair) is neuter, but
       <i>
        Tien un pel
        <u>
         u
        </u>
        rox
        <u>
         u
        </u>
       </i>
       (He has
       <i>
        a
       </i>
       red hair) is masculine; note the noun's change in ending.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Number">
        <span id="Singular_and_plural">
        </span>
        Number
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Asturian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Number">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       Plural formation is complex:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Masculine nouns ending in
        <i>
         -u
        </i>
        →
        <i>
         -os
        </i>
        :
        <i>
         texu
        </i>
        (yew) →
        <i>
         texos
        </i>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        Feminine nouns ending in
        <i>
         -a
        </i>
        →
        <i>
         -es
        </i>
        :
        <i>
         vaca
        </i>
        (cow) →
        <i>
         vaques
        </i>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        Masculine or feminine nouns ending in a consonant take
        <i>
         -es
        </i>
        :
        <i>
         animal
        </i>
        (animal) →
        <i>
         animales; xabón
        </i>
        (soap) →
        <i>
         xabones
        </i>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        Words ending in
        <i>
         -z
        </i>
        may take a masculine
        <i>
         -os
        </i>
        to distinguish them from the feminine plural:
        <i>
         rapaz
        </i>
        (boy) →
        <i>
         rapazos
        </i>
        ;
        <i>
         rapaza
        </i>
        (girl) →
        <i>
         rapaces
        </i>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        Masculine nouns ending in
        <i>
         -ín
        </i>
        →
        <i>
         -inos
        </i>
        :
        <i>
         camín
        </i>
        (way, path) →
        <i>
         caminos
        </i>
        , re-establishing the etymological vowel.
       </li>
       <li>
        Feminine nouns ending in
        <i>
         -á
        </i>
        ,
        <i>
         -ada
        </i>
        ,
        <i>
         -ú
        </i>
        →
        <i>
         -aes
        </i>
        or
        <i>
         -úes
        </i>
        , also re-establishing the etymological vowel:
        <i>
         ciudá
        </i>
        (city) →
        <i>
         ciudaes; cansada
        </i>
        (tired [feminine]) →
        <i>
         cansaes; virtú
        </i>
        (virtue) →
        <i>
         virtúes
        </i>
        .
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Determiners">
        Determiners
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Asturian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Determiners">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       Their forms are:
      </p>
      <div>
       <table class="multicol" role="presentation" style="border-collapse: collapse; padding: 0; border: 0; background:transparent; width:100%;">
        <tr>
         <td style="width:50%; text-align:left; vertical-align:top;">
          <table class="wikitable" style="text-align:center;">
           <caption>
            Definite article
           </caption>
           <tr>
            <th rowspan="2">
            </th>
            <th colspan="3">
             Singular
            </th>
            <th colspan="2">
             Plural
            </th>
           </tr>
           <tr>
            <th>
             masc.
            </th>
            <th>
             fem.
            </th>
            <th>
             neuter
            </th>
            <th>
             masc.
            </th>
            <th>
             fem.
            </th>
           </tr>
           <tr align="center">
            <td>
             <b>
              Before cons
             </b>
            </td>
            <td>
             el
            </td>
            <td>
             la
            </td>
            <td rowspan="2">
             lo
            </td>
            <td rowspan="2">
             los
            </td>
            <td rowspan="2">
             les
            </td>
           </tr>
           <tr align="center">
            <td>
             <b>
              Before vowel
             </b>
            </td>
            <td>
             l'
            </td>
            <td>
             la / l'
             <sup>
              *
             </sup>
            </td>
           </tr>
          </table>
         </td>
         <td style="width:50%; text-align:left; vertical-align:top;">
          <table class="wikitable" style="text-align:center;">
           <caption>
            Indefinite article
           </caption>
           <tr>
            <th colspan="2">
             Singular
            </th>
            <th colspan="2">
             Plural
            </th>
           </tr>
           <tr>
            <th>
             masc.
            </th>
            <th>
             fem.
            </th>
            <th>
             masc.
            </th>
            <th>
             fem.
            </th>
           </tr>
           <tr align="center">
            <td>
             un
            </td>
            <td>
             una
            </td>
            <td>
             unos
            </td>
            <td>
             unes
            </td>
           </tr>
          </table>
         </td>
        </tr>
       </table>
      </div>
      <p>
       <sup>
        *
       </sup>
       Only before words beginning with
       <i>
        a-
       </i>
       :
       <i>
        l’aigla
       </i>
       (the eagle),
       <i>
        l’alma
       </i>
       (the soul). Compare
       <i>
        la entrada
       </i>
       (the entry) and
       <i>
        la islla
       </i>
       (the island).
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Vocabulary">
        Vocabulary
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Asturian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Vocabulary">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Like other Romance languages, most Asturian words come from
       <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">
        Latin
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        ablana, agua, falar, güeyu, home, llibru, muyer, pesllar, pexe, prau, suañar
       </i>
       . In addition to this Latin basis are words which entered Asturian from languages spoken before the arrival of Latin (its
       <a href="/wiki/Stratum_(linguistics)" title="Stratum (linguistics)">
        substratum
       </a>
       ), afterwards (its superstratum) and
       <a href="/wiki/Loanword" title="Loanword">
        loanwords
       </a>
       from other languages.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Substratum">
        Substratum
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Asturian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Substratum">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       Although little is known about the language of the ancient
       <a href="/wiki/Astures" title="Astures">
        Astures
       </a>
       , it may have been related to two
       <a href="/wiki/Indo-European_languages" title="Indo-European languages">
        Indo-European languages
       </a>
       :
       <a href="/wiki/Celtic_languages" title="Celtic languages">
        Celtic
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Lusitanian_language" title="Lusitanian language">
        Lusitanian
       </a>
       . Words from this language and the pre–Indo-European languages spoken in the region are known as the prelatinian substratum; examples include
       <i>
        bedul, boroña, brincar, bruxa, cándanu, cantu, carrascu, comba, cuetu, güelga, llamuerga, llastra, llócara, matu, peñera, riega, tapín
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        zucar
       </i>
       . Many Celtic words (such as
       <i>
        bragues, camisa, carru, cerveza
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        sayu
       </i>
       ) were integrated into Latin and, later, into Asturian.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Superstratum">
        Superstratum
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Asturian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Superstratum">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       Asturian's superstratum consists primarily of
       <a href="/wiki/Germanism_(linguistics)" title="Germanism (linguistics)">
        Germanisms
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabism" title="Arabism">
        Arabisms
       </a>
       . The Germanic peoples in the Iberian Peninsula, especially the
       <a href="/wiki/Visigoths" title="Visigoths">
        Visigoths
       </a>
       and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Suevi" title="Suevi">
        Suevi
       </a>
       , added words such as
       <i>
        blancu, esquila, estaca, mofu, serón, espetar, gadañu
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        tosquilar
       </i>
       . Arabisms could reach Asturian directly, through contacts with Arabs or
       <a href="/wiki/Al-Andalus" title="Al-Andalus">
        al-Andalus
       </a>
       , or through the Castilian language. Examples include
       <i>
        acebache, alfaya, altafarra, bañal, ferre, galbana, mandil, safase, xabalín, zuna
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        zucre
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Loanwords">
        <span id="Loans">
        </span>
        Loanwords
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Asturian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Loanwords">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       Asturian has also received much of its lexicon from other languages, such as
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
        Castilian
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">
        French
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Occitan" title="Occitan">
        Occitan
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Galician_language" title="Galician language">
        Galician
       </a>
       . In number of loanwords, Spanish leads the list. However, due to the relationship between Castilian and the Asturian it is unclear if a word is borrowed from Castilian, common to both languages from Latin or a loanword from Asturian to Castilian. Some Castilian forms in Asturian are:
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <dl>
         <dd>
          <table class="wikitable">

             </i>
            </td>
           </tr>
           <tr>
            <th>
             <a href="/wiki/Galician_language" title="Galician language">
              Galician

             </i>
            </td>

         </dd>
        </dl>

       <span class="mw-headline" id="Lexical_comparison">
        Lexical comparison
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
